PRIME GAP RESONANCE PROJECT: 250-PAGE PURE TEXT BREAKDOWN
VERSION: PGR-250-A4-TEXT-2026-05-13

Pagination note:
This is a pure text file with explicit PAGE markers and form-feed page breaks. Exact A4 pagination depends on font, margins, and editor settings. The content is organized as 250 A4-style pages rather than as a typeset PDF. The mathematical status labels follow the supplied project ledger.

Global caution:
This document is a research ledger and breakdown, not a proof of the original positive problem and not a proof of the all-alpha no-positive-limit theorem.

PAGE 001 OF 250
TITLE: Project identity
STATUS: STRUCTURAL / OVERVIEW
OBJECT: Prime Gap Resonance Project

SUMMARY:
The project studies selected normalized prime gaps along Bohr-type windows determined by an
irrational alpha. The central selected average is A_alpha(x), formed by weighting primes p
with the sharp moving selector 1_{||alpha p||<1/log p} and averaging the normalized gap
g(p).

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project has produced a large reduction architecture, a metric theorem according to the
ledger, and a precise catalogue of structural obstructions. The main achievement is not a
positive construction or a universal negative theorem, but a disciplined map of what either
direction must overcome.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The project separates actual sharp moving selectors from frozen, smoothed, hidden Bernoulli,
and finite-stage models. It also separates full gaps from clipped gaps, tails, threshold
indicators, tuple arrays, and local rectangle statistics. This separation is the reason
later endpoint claims can be audited instead of guessed.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page introduces the whole ledger. Every later page refines a branch, endpoint, or
analytic engine.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
The original positive problem remains open: no irrational alpha with A_alpha(x) tending to
L0>1 has been constructed. The all-alpha no-positive-limit theorem also remains open.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'Project identity', the success criterion is not rhetorical agreement but a
status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic, it
can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows the search space
without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the implication is usable only
after the named engines are supplied. If it is marked OPEN, the page identifies a target
rather than a conclusion.

DEPENDENCIES AND FAILURE MODES:
This page should be read together with the selector discipline, gap discipline, and range
discipline of the project. A common failure mode is to use the object 'Prime Gap Resonance
Project' in a nearby but different normalization, selector, cutoff, residue class, or
averaging regime. Another failure mode is to replace an L2, U2, or BDH-type statement by a
first-moment statement. Those replacements are not harmless unless a separate lemma proves
them.

CONTINUATION NOTES:
A future continuation agent can use this page as a ledger entry by preserving the status
label 'STRUCTURAL / OVERVIEW' and then adding only genuinely new proof, disproof, or
reduction content. If a new argument changes the status, it should state exactly which
assumptions were removed or which endpoint was proved. Otherwise the page remains part of
the dependency map, not a solved component.

CHECKLIST FOR USING THIS PAGE:
Before citing this page in a theorem, verify five items: the selector is the intended
selector; the averaged object is the intended gap, tuple, pair, rectangle, or cube object;
the normalization and range are the same as in the target theorem; all boundary, collision,
W-trick, and prime-power transfers are either irrelevant or explicitly included; and the
final claim does not exceed the status label. This checklist is deliberately repetitive
because most false upgrades fail in exactly one of these places.

DISCIPLINE / CAUTION:

PAGE 002 OF 250
TITLE: Global status in one page
STATUS: OPEN / PROVEN / CONDITIONAL MIX
OBJECT: A_alpha(x), finite-type alpha, metric alpha

SUMMARY:
There are three top-level statuses. Positive existence is open. The universal all-alpha
negative theorem is open. The metric theorem A_alpha(x)->1 for Lebesgue-a.e. irrational
alpha is recorded as proven in the project ledger.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The metric theorem is the strongest clean global theorem. It shows typical alpha do not
produce a positive limiting bias. The project then asks whether exceptional alpha, finite-
type or Liouville, can support a stable positive selected mean.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The finite-type negative route is conditional. It reduces any positive-limit branch to named
endpoint engines. In the s=2 rational-major subbranch, those endpoints have been compressed
to one analytic equivalence class centered on rectangle-BDH / centered pair-cube /
anisotropic U^3.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page is the status dashboard for the whole project.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
The analytic endpoint remains open. The finite-type theorem is not unconditional. Liouville
and large-range branches remain separate and unresolved.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'Global status in one page', the success criterion is not rhetorical agreement
but a status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic,

PAGE 003 OF 250
TITLE: Main selector warning
STATUS: REQUIRED DISCIPLINE
OBJECT: chi_alpha(p)=1_{||alpha p||<1/log p}

SUMMARY:
The actual selector is sharp and moving. It depends on p through the boundary 1/log p. Many
useful intermediate results use frozen, smoothed, finite-band, or probabilistic versions,
but those are not the original problem.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project succeeded in making selector discipline explicit. This prevents common invalid
upgrades from a smoothed dyadic statement to the actual moving selector theorem.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Any transfer from a smoothed or frozen model to the actual selector must include boundary
transfer, moving-window control, prefix safety, denominator control, tail control, and
sharp-window transition estimates. Without those, the result belongs only to its model.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page guards the gateway between model statements and the actual problem.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
A complete positive construction for the actual selector remains open. A universal negative
theorem for the actual selector remains open.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'Main selector warning', the success criterion is not rhetorical agreement but
a status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic, it
can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows the search space
without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the implication is usable only
after the named engines are supplied. If it is marked OPEN, the page identifies a target
rather than a conclusion.

DEPENDENCIES AND FAILURE MODES:

PAGE 004 OF 250
TITLE: Gap decomposition warning
STATUS: REQUIRED DISCIPLINE
OBJECT: g(p), g_H(p), tau_H(p)

SUMMARY:
The selected average uses full normalized prime gaps. Most reductions split the gap into a
clipped part g_H(p)=min(g(p),H) and a tail tau_H(p)=(g(p)-H)_+.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project succeeded in routing positive-limit behavior through clipped covariance or tail
covariance. This is the master split that lets bounded Fourier methods treat one side and
tail/threshold analysis treat the other.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The clipped branch becomes a bounded array problem. The tail branch becomes a threshold and
empty-interval problem. Both need separate endpoint engines. Treating global mean-one prime
gaps as local uniform integrability is explicitly blocked.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page explains why full gaps cannot be handled by a single bounded-array theorem.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Local tail uniformity, high-count Bonferroni control, and large-range escape remain open in
the relevant branches.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'Gap decomposition warning', the success criterion is not rhetorical agreement
but a status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic,
it can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows the search
space without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the implication is usable
only after the named engines are supplied. If it is marked OPEN, the page identifies a
target rather than a conclusion.

DEPENDENCIES AND FAILURE MODES:
This page should be read together with the selector discipline, gap discipline, and range
discipline of the project. A common failure mode is to use the object 'g(p), g_H(p),
tau_H(p)' in a nearby but different normalization, selector, cutoff, residue class, or
averaging regime. Another failure mode is to replace an L2, U2, or BDH-type statement by a
first-moment statement. Those replacements are not harmless unless a separate lemma proves
them.

CONTINUATION NOTES:

PAGE 005 OF 250
TITLE: Success summary
STATUS: STRUCTURAL SUCCESS
OBJECT: Reductions, calibrations, endpoint compression

SUMMARY:
The project has not solved the original open problem, but it has achieved substantial
structural compression. The strongest concrete success is the reduction of the s=2 rational-
major branch to one analytic endpoint equivalence class.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
Finite-local singular calibrations, divisor-cover formulas, nonsquarefree denominator
vanishing, rectangle local models, two-rectangle local models, covariance comb bounds,
prime-power transfer, dyadic conversion, and margin absorption are all recorded as proven or
deterministic within the ledger.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The analytic endpoint can be stated as RBDH^{pair}_{short}(H), CPC_3^sharp(H), shifted-pair
spectral U^2, dyadic derivative U^2, or anisotropic U^3. These are equivalent modulo side
packages.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page records the distinction between progress and proof, since confusing those is how
projects become folklore.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
The endpoint itself remains open. The success is compression, not closure.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:

PAGE 006 OF 250
TITLE: Current best analytic target
STATUS: OPEN ANALYTIC ENGINE
OBJECT: RBDH^{pair}_{short}(H) / CPC_3^sharp(H)

SUMMARY:
The best compressed target in the s=2 rational-major branch is a rectangle-BDH estimate for
shifted-prime-pair autocorrelations, equivalently a centered pair-cube fourth moment.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The endpoint is explicit: average over short shifts d and long shifts h of the square of the
difference between a four-prime rectangle count and its exact local model Sigma_w(d,h).

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The model is not kappa_w(d)^2. It is Sigma_w(d,h), the product over p>w of the four-root
local opportunity factor for 0, -d, -h, -h-d. This exact model removes the local covariance
comb.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page gives the present analytic battlefield.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Proving this estimate in the required H-range remains open. The required H-range must be
read from the finite-type reduction.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:

PAGE 007 OF 250
TITLE: Original positive problem
STATUS: OPEN
OBJECT: Existence of alpha with A_alpha(x)->L0>1

SUMMARY:
The positive problem asks whether some irrational alpha can force a stable selected
normalized prime-gap average above one. Sparse planting gives resonant large gaps but not a
stable finite limit.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project clarified why planting spikes is insufficient. Cesaro rigidity, leakage, prefix
safety, post-window combs, and moving-selector transfer all obstruct naive construction
methods.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Any positive construction must control denominator divergence, scalar feedback, prefix
safety, boundary transfer, tail behavior, transition control, and irrational survivor
extraction. None of these requirements has been fully met.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page records that positive existence is not disproved, merely constrained.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
No positive construction for the actual sharp moving selector is available in the ledger.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'Original positive problem', the success criterion is not rhetorical agreement
but a status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic,
it can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows the search
space without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the implication is usable
only after the named engines are supplied. If it is marked OPEN, the page identifies a
target rather than a conclusion.

DEPENDENCIES AND FAILURE MODES:
This page should be read together with the selector discipline, gap discipline, and range
discipline of the project. A common failure mode is to use the object 'Existence of alpha
with A_alpha(x)->L0>1' in a nearby but different normalization, selector, cutoff, residue
class, or averaging regime. Another failure mode is to replace an L2, U2, or BDH-type
statement by a first-moment statement. Those replacements are not harmless unless a separate
lemma proves them.

CONTINUATION NOTES:

PAGE 008 OF 250
TITLE: Universal negative problem
STATUS: OPEN
OBJECT: All irrational alpha

SUMMARY:
The all-alpha theorem would say no irrational alpha can have A_alpha(x)->L0>1. The project
has not proved this. It has proved or recorded metric typical behavior and conditional
finite-type reductions.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The main success toward the negative direction is structural: any positive finite limit must
create obstruction branches. For finite-type alpha, those branches are conditionally
eliminated under endpoint engines.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Exceptional alpha remain dangerous. Liouville short-comb plateaus, singular survivor
measures, and large-range escape can evade finite-type methods.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page prevents the metric theorem from being misread as a universal theorem.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
The universal theorem needs deterministic decorrelation, denominator control, tail control,
boundary transfer, sharp-window control, Liouville comb analysis, and prefix engines.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'Universal negative problem', the success criterion is not rhetorical
agreement but a status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or
deterministic, it can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows
the search space without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the
implication is usable only after the named engines are supplied. If it is marked OPEN, the
page identifies a target rather than a conclusion.

moment statement. Those replacements are not harmless unless a separate lemma proves them.

PAGE 009 OF 250
TITLE: Metric theorem
STATUS: PROVEN ACCORDING TO PROJECT LEDGER
OBJECT: Lebesgue-a.e. irrational alpha

SUMMARY:
For Lebesgue-a.e. irrational alpha, the selected average A_alpha(x) tends to 1. This is the
strongest clean global theorem in the ledger.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The result is supported by maximal metric sampling for L2-controlled arrays, bounded-array
no-bias statements, and sublinear prime-gap input for the full-gap transfer.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The theorem handles typical alpha. It does not classify exceptional alpha. It also does not
construct positive examples or prove they cannot exist.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page marks the main unconditional global success of the project ledger.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Exceptional finite-type and Liouville cases remain outside the metric theorem. The project
continues by analyzing these branches structurally.

TITLE: Finite-type negative route
STATUS: CONDITIONAL
OBJECT: Irrational alpha of finite Diophantine type

SUMMARY:
The finite-type route aims to prove that no finite positive limit can exist for finite-type
alpha. The proof is conditional on endpoint engines.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The route has been compressed through covariance extraction, clipped/tail routing, rational-
major analysis, divisor projection, and finally the s=2 endpoint equivalence class.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The current s=2 branch can be closed if RBDH^{pair}_{short}(H), or equivalently
CPC_3^sharp(H) or AU^3(H), is proved in all ranges extracted by the reduction, along with
transfer packages.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page states the conditional nature of the finite-type program.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
The endpoint engine remains open. Large-range escape also remains open if extracted ranges
exceed the engine range.

TITLE: Large-range escape
STATUS: OPEN
OBJECT: Ranges outside subpower / engine coverage

SUMMARY:
Large-range escape occurs when parameters such as H, q, W, eta^{-1}, or shape complexity
exceed the regime in which carrier sparsity, high-count closure, or finite-type exclusions
are known.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project succeeded in naming this escape rather than burying it inside a hidden
quantifier. This is important because endpoint engines are range-dependent.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
If the single s=2 engine is proved only for H<=mathcal H(N), and the reduction produces
D>mathcal H(N), the branch is not closed. It is routed to large-range control.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page records range honesty.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Large-range control is open. It may require different analytic tools from the short-shift
endpoint.

PAGE 015 OF 250
TITLE: Prime gaps and normalization
STATUS: DEFINITION
OBJECT: Delta_n, g_n, g(p)

SUMMARY:
The normalized prime gap is g_n=(p_{n+1}-p_n)/log p_n, or g(p)=(p^+-p)/log p in prime-
variable notation. This normalization makes the global mean tend to one.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The normalization lets the project ask whether selection by a Bohr window can bias the mean
gap above the global baseline. It also supports clipped/tail decomposition.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The global average of normalized gaps tends to one, but local selected averages may deviate.
The project studies whether such deviations can stabilize for exceptional alpha.

WHERE IT FITS:
This is the numerical quantity averaged throughout the project.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Local selected behavior is not determined by the global mean. Tail uniformity and selector
correlation remain hard.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:

PAGE 016 OF 250
TITLE: Actual selected denominator
STATUS: DEFINITION
OBJECT: D_alpha(x)

SUMMARY:
The selected denominator is D_alpha(x)=sum_{p<=x} chi_alpha(p), where
chi_alpha(p)=1_{||alpha p||<1/log p}.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
Tracking the denominator is essential. A positive limiting average means nothing if the
denominator is too sparse, unstable, or subject to prefix domination.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Many reductions condition on D_alpha(x)->infinity. Finite convergence also imposes Cesaro
rigidity on selected gaps: selected spikes must be prefix-safe and cannot dominate too late.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page isolates the denominator from the numerator.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Denominator asymptotics for exceptional alpha remain a major transfer issue.

TITLE: Actual selected numerator
STATUS: DEFINITION
OBJECT: N_alpha(x)

SUMMARY:
The selected numerator is N_alpha(x)=sum_{p<=x} chi_alpha(p)g(p). The average is
A_alpha(x)=N_alpha(x)/D_alpha(x) whenever D_alpha(x)>0.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
This direct definition keeps the project honest: all model and smoothed results must return
to this numerator if they claim anything about the original problem.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The numerator is decomposed into clipped and tail parts. Positive excess above one must
appear in clipped covariance or tail covariance after q-centering.

OBJECT: m^q_{X,H}, a^q_{X,H}

TITLE: Clipped gaps
STATUS: DEFINITION
OBJECT: g_H(p)=min(g(p),H)

Clipped gaps are bounded. This makes them accessible to Fourier and bounded-array sampling
methods.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The clipped branch is where classical bounded Fourier decorrelation has the best chance to
work. It routes to threshold layers, empty intervals, tuples, and high-count alternatives.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:

boundary packages must handle the resulting thresholds.

TITLE: Tail gaps
STATUS: DEFINITION
OBJECT: tau_H(p)=(g(p)-H)_+

The tail carries large-gap mass above H. It is unbounded and cannot be treated as a fixed

offset Fourier, high-count, and large-range control.

PAGE 022 OF 250
TITLE: Empty intervals
STATUS: DEFINITION
OBJECT: g(p)>t

SUMMARY:
The condition g(p)>t means that the interval (p,p+t log p] contains no prime. This converts
gap thresholds into empty-interval statements.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
Empty intervals allow use of tuple-count expansions and Bonferroni-type high-count analysis.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The project repeatedly routes tail and clipped threshold covariance into Fourier estimates
involving empty intervals and local prime-cluster indicators.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page links gap thresholds to local prime patterns.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
High-count remainders and growing-order tuple neutrality remain barriers.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:

status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic, it
can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows the search space
without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the implication is usable only

PAGE 023 OF 250
TITLE: Tuple counts
STATUS: DEFINITION
OBJECT: Y_p(h), E_p(h), B_{p,j}(h)

SUMMARY:
Y_p(h) counts primes q with p<q<=p+h. E_p(h)=1_{Y_p(h)=0}; B_{p,j}(h)=binom(Y_p(h),j).

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
These arrays support Bonferroni expansions of empty-interval indicators and allow high-count
clusters to be isolated.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Fixed-order tuple neutrality is proven in finite-local settings, but growing-order
neutrality is much harder and must not be assumed.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page defines the local tuple language.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
High-count cluster bounds remain part of the clipped and tail branch endpoint package.

TITLE: Selector taxonomy
STATUS: REQUIRED DISCIPLINE
OBJECT: sharp, frozen, smoothed, Bernoulli, finite-stage

SUMMARY:
The project distinguishes the actual sharp moving selector, sharp frozen dyadic selector,
smoothed finite-band frozen selector, hidden Bernoulli lift, finite-stage reference
measures, and survivor/core-floor measures.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
This taxonomy prevents model drift. A theorem for a smoothed finite-band selector is useful,
but it is not a theorem for chi_alpha unless transfer hypotheses are included.

moving-selector theorem. The project explicitly forbids this.

TITLE: Forbidden upgrades
STATUS: REQUIRED DISCIPLINE
OBJECT: No metric-to-all-alpha, no spike-to-limit

SUMMARY:
The project forbids confusing almost-everywhere convergence with all-alpha convergence,
residual spikes with finite limits, or sparse planting with stable positive construction.

reasoning are blocked.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:

sharp moving-selector results, treating first moments as BDH variance, treating global mean
as local uniform integrability, and ignoring singular-series covariance.

TITLE: W-trick limit order
STATUS: REQUIRED STRUCTURE
OBJECT: N first, w second

SUMMARY:
The W-trick uses W=prod_{p<=w}p. Finite-local statements usually take N->infty for fixed w,
then w->infty, implemented by choosing w(N) slowly.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
This limit order is essential for local model suppression and residue equidistribution.
Letting W grow too fast can destroy interval length and boundary estimates.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
All endpoint engines require W=N^{o(1)} unless a stronger regime is explicitly proved.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page sets the W-trick operating rules.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Uniformity in w remains part of the analytic burden.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'W-trick limit order', the success criterion is not rhetorical agreement but a
status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic, it
can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows the search space
without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the implication is usable only
after the named engines are supplied. If it is marked OPEN, the page identifies a target
rather than a conclusion.

TITLE: Range parameter
STATUS: REQUIRED STRUCTURE
OBJECT: mathcal H(N)

SUMMARY:
Endpoint engines are parameterized by the short-shift range H<=mathcal H(N), or dyadic

TITLE: Sparse planting
STATUS: PROVEN
OBJECT: infinitely many resonant primes

SUMMARY:
For sufficiently sparse primes P_j, one can construct irrational alpha with ||alpha
P_j||<1/log P_j for all j.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
This proves that resonance spikes can be planted. It shows exceptional alpha can be forced

control, and denominator transition control.

PAGE 047 OF 250
TITLE: Cesaro rigidity
STATUS: PROVEN
OBJECT: finite selected mean constraint

SUMMARY:
If a selected nonnegative sequence has finite Cesaro mean, then individual selected terms
must be o(k) relative to selected count. For prime gaps, selected g(p)=o(D_alpha(p)).

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
This blocks constructions that rely on isolated huge gaps to force a finite stable limit.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The result does not prevent all positive limits. It says any positive limit construction
must be prefix-safe and distributed, not spike-driven.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page records a fundamental obstruction to sparse planting.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
A distributed positive construction remains open.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:

OBJECT: Cesaro rigidity

SUMMARY:
Large isolated selected gaps can create limsup spikes, but finite Cesaro convergence
requires selected terms to be small relative to selected count.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project succeeded in translating this elementary Cesaro fact into a prime-gap
constraint: if A_alpha(x) tends to a finite L, then selected gaps cannot grow like the
selected denominator.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
This kills naive constructions where the entire positive bias is carried by rare massive
gaps.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page explains why limsup infinity is not a positive finite limit.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Distributed positive bias remains possible in principle and open.

IMPLICATIONS FOR PROJECT SUCCESS:
For the topic 'Why spikes fail as limits', the success criterion is not rhetorical agreement
but a status-preserving mathematical advance. If the page is marked PROVEN or deterministic,
it can be used as a stable dependency. If it is marked STRUCTURAL, it narrows the search
space without eliminating the branch. If it is marked CONDITIONAL, the implication is usable
only after the named engines are supplied. If it is marked OPEN, the page identifies a
target rather than a conclusion.

DEPENDENCIES AND FAILURE MODES:
This page should be read together with the selector discipline, gap discipline, and range
discipline of the project. A common failure mode is to use the object 'Cesaro rigidity' in a
nearby but different normalization, selector, cutoff, residue class, or averaging regime.
Another failure mode is to replace an L2, U2, or BDH-type statement by a first-moment

PAGE 057 OF 250
TITLE: Leakage problem
STATUS: STRUCTURAL WARNING
OBJECT: selection spillover

SUMMARY:
A planted alpha rarely selects only the intended primes. Nearby rational approximations can
create additional selected primes in comb-like post-windows.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project identifies leakage as a central obstruction for positive construction. Any
actual construction must control both planted mass and unintended background mass.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Leakage can dilute or destabilize the selected average. It also disrupts denominator control
and prefix safety.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page focuses on background selection.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
No construction currently controls leakage sufficiently for A_alpha(x)->L0>1.

PAGE 058 OF 250
TITLE: Prefix safety
STATUS: REQUIRED FOR POSITIVE CONSTRUCTION
OBJECT: early selected denominator

SUMMARY:
A positive finite limit cannot be driven by late spikes that overwhelm earlier selected
mass. Prefix safety means every construction stage must preserve the long-term average
target without being destroyed by earlier or later selections.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project succeeded in naming prefix safety as a mandatory condition rather than a
cosmetic refinement.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Prefix safety interacts with denominator growth, large gaps, and tail exclusion. It is
especially hard for sparse or stagewise constructions.

WHERE IT FITS:

TITLE: Master covariance theorem
STATUS: PROVEN STRUCTURAL / EXTRACTION
OBJECT: Theorem 85.1

SUMMARY:
If A_alpha(x) tends to 1+delta and D_alpha(x) diverges, then for every fixed H either
clipped covariance or tail covariance occurs on positive selected-denominator mass
infinitely often.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
This is the central structural obstruction theorem. It turns a limiting selected average
into named local failures.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
The theorem uses q-centered shell means for g_H and tau_H and the dyadic q-weighted full-gap
mean tending to one.

This page states the master split.

TITLE: Clipped covariance
STATUS: STRUCTURAL BRANCH
OBJECT: C^{clip,q}_{X,H}

SUMMARY:
The clipped covariance is sum chi_alpha(p)(g_H(p)-m^q_{X,H}) over a dyadic shell. It is
bounded because g_H is bounded.

TITLE: Tail covariance
STATUS: STRUCTURAL BRANCH
OBJECT: C^{tail,q}_{X,H}

SUMMARY:
Tail covariance is sum chi_alpha(p)(tau_H(p)-a^q_{X,H}). It carries large-gap contributions
above H.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
Tail covariance is harder because tau_H is unbounded. It must be routed through threshold

still need analysis.

TITLE: Tail layer-cake
STATUS: STRUCTURAL
OBJECT: tail covariance to thresholds

TITLE: Prefix-dangerous exclusion
STATUS: PROVEN
OBJECT: large y compared to D_alpha

PAGE 211 OF 250
TITLE: What is not yet success
STATUS: SYNTHESIS
OBJECT: blocked overclaims

SUMMARY:
It is not success to prove a smoothed finite-stage theorem and call it actual selector
convergence. It is not success to show spikes and call them finite positive limits. It is
not success to prove first-moment rectangle HL and call it rectangle-BDH.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The ledger has become stricter over time. It blocks exactly these tempting overclaims.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
A real proof must account for selector transfer, local models, variance not just means,
boundary strips, collision hyperplanes, W-trick limits, and range coverage.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page protects the project from premature conclusions.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Those requirements remain in force.

OBJECT: RBDH^{pair}_{short}(mathcal H)

SUMMARY:

TITLE: Why RBDH is variance-strength
STATUS: STRUCTURAL
OBJECT: second moment not first moment

SUMMARY:
Rectangle-BDH is an L2_h variance estimate. It cannot be replaced by mean rectangle Hardy-
Littlewood estimates.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
The project proved model obstructions: a phase in h has small mean but large L2 mass.

This is why any route must control spectral density, autocorrelation square, centered cube,
or WHL8-type quadratic expansion.

PAGE 218 OF 250
TITLE: Exact model Sigma_w
STATUS: PROVEN FINITE-LOCAL
OBJECT: rectangle singular model

SUMMARY:
The exact rectangle model is Sigma_w(d,h)=prod_{p>w}(1-1/p)^{-4}(1-rho_p(d,h)/p), where
rho_p counts the distinct roots 0,-d,-h,-h-d modulo p.

SUCCESS / ACHIEVEMENT:
This model is one of the major finite-local successes of the late modules.

TECHNICAL BREAKDOWN:
Replacing Sigma_w by kappa_w(d)^2 leaves an AP-tooth covariance comb. The comb is harmless
in L2 but not pointwise.

WHERE IT FITS:
This page records the exact model.

WHAT REMAINS OPEN:
Analytic estimates must subtract Sigma_w first.

TITLE: Pair model kappa_w
STATUS: PROVEN FINITE-LOCAL
OBJECT: shifted-pair singular model

SUMMARY:
The pair model is kappa_w(d)=prod_{p>w}(1-1/p)^{-2}(1-#{0,-d}/p). It is the correct mean for
P_d(n)=nu(n+d)nu(n).

Subtracting kappa_w removes the zero-frequency pair main term from shifted-pair spectral U2.

sense.
